    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

  <span id="freeText3677756010940157927" style="display:none">'A worthy successor to '1984' and 'Brave New World'' - PLAYBOY <br /><br />What would I do for eternal life? Discoveries made within our lifetime will allow people to remain young forever. There is no more death. Our children will never die. Welcome to a world inhabited by people who are perfectly healthy, beautiful and eternally young. Every utopia has its shadowy backstreets. Someone has to make sure that overpopulation doesn't bring the wonderful world of the future crashing down. Someone has to make people forget their animal instincts and live in a fitting way for immortals. Maybe that someone is me? <br /><br />The utopia "FUTU.RE" is the first novel after five years' silence from Dmitry Glukhovksy, author of the cult novel "METRO 2033." The author's books have been translated into dozens of foreign languages, selling in millions of copies, and have been adapted for the big screen in Hollywood - but none of them will grip you like "FUTU.RE"</span>

    That`s good question. I think that maybe it was a lie that no one can get out from the internat after failing the trial - cause regimes prefer to be s<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    That`s good question. I think that maybe it was a lie that no one can get out from the internat after failing the trial - cause regimes prefer to be seen as more opressive than they are. They just wanted them to be scared of such possibility - but also needed new Immortal to work. <br />Or, another solution coming to my mind - it was Schreyer himself who get out 503 from internat in order to motivate/test/play with Jan.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13238416418614566259">This book was like Huxley, Orwell, Atwood, plus a couple more folks had a baby together and it came out as an instant angsty teen with anger and anxiety issues, kicking garbage bins, starting fights with boys and calling girls whores, and who kept overdosing his meds and because of that was losing his memory all the time and as a result he was repeating same rants over and over. <br/><br/>This book was almost an ordeal, if it wasn't for the audio I would probably dnf, even if this was Glukhovsky whom I re</span>
  <span id="freeText13238416418614566259" style="display:none">This book was like Huxley, Orwell, Atwood, plus a couple more folks had a baby together and it came out as an instant angsty teen with anger and anxiety issues, kicking garbage bins, starting fights with boys and calling girls whores, and who kept overdosing his meds and because of that was losing his memory all the time and as a result he was repeating same rants over and over. <br /><br />This book was almost an ordeal, if it wasn't for the audio I would probably dnf, even if this was Glukhovsky whom I really like and appreciate. The writing was good, it truly impressed, but other things...<br />My problem wasn't that this book depicted violent and ruthless world and the main character was equally violent and unsympathetic abortion commando. It's dystopia and the rules were set by the author and he had that right to make it what he wanted. If his intention was to show the heartless rotten society and rapey characters - who am I to tell him not to, even if I didn't particularly enjoy it. I knew what I was getting into and I didn't expect fluffy unicorns shitting rainbows here. <br /><br />My problem was that Glukhovsky borrowed from many authors - the ones I already mentioned plus others I might now not exactly recall by names - but he tried so hard to make it look like this was the first dystopia ever written! Like, seriously, dude, we've seen this all already before, we've read this before, did you just wake up from 30 years long coma? He won't surprise you with some fresh ideas, unless this is indeed your first  dystopian novel and you're like 14 y.o. In which case yes, it will blow your mind. In many ways. <br />Supposedly unexpected plot twists, especially one in the end - completely predictable, if you were a careful reader, also more suitable for "Telemundo presenta" than something signed by this author, imho. Philosophic "discoveries" made by protagonist - too obvious and I would've been completely OK with them, but he kept repeating those enlighted monologues again and again like the reader was dumb, not the protagonist making those discoveries. <br />Then this - now I will call my mama a whore, now I will forgive her, now I will call her a whore again, now I will forgive her, and so on. Annelie (not sure if I'm spelling it right) is a whore, Annelie is a saint, Annelie is a whore, Annelie is a saint, and so on...<br />Then that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[baby in the end <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>... I'll stop it right here, don't want to spoil, but it was also quite predictable. <br />So yeah, colour me utterly disappointed. Maybe if it was shorter by half, I could appreciate the idea and Glukhovsky's usual wit but it all drowned in the sea of annoyance that this novel was.<br /><br />P.S. Also, I don't need to waste my empathy for dystopian future forced abortion when there's governmental one in China in our very real today.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13238416418614566259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14274560641016663628" style="display:none">TINY SPOILERS.<br /><br />After the amazing Metro 2033 and 2034 novels this one was a disappointment. First of all, the idea is repeated. I have read a sci fi story with immortal society and purity squads hunting those who want to have children at least a years ago in one of Paolo Bacigalupi's Windup Stories. Also - I really hoped that Dmitry Glukhovsky would amaze me and make me wonder philosophically about the human nature (like it happened with Metros). But he didn't. The only feeling I had was disappointment. It was totally predictable in one aspect: every pretty woman the main hero encounters will be either raped by someone, forced to have him with pain at her servile consent or simply taken to bed (the F word would suit here better actually). Predictable, boring and painful. The future world in Glukhovsky's vision is a very bad place for women. <br />I'm disappointed and sad. Hopefully Metro 2035 will be a better book. <br /><br />I won't read Futu.re vol. 2 if it ever appears. </span>

<div id="review_1638523813" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1638523813" />
    <a title="Sad Sunday (If I say it&#39;s bad, it&#39;s bad)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22985424-sad-sunday-if-i-say-it-s-bad-it-s-bad"><img alt="Sad Sunday (If I say it&#39;s bad, it&#39;s bad)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544800600p2/22985424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1638523813?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sad Sunday (If I say it&#39;s bad, it&#39;s bad)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sad Sunday (If I say it&#39;s bad, it&#39;s bad)" href="/user/show/22985424-sad-sunday-if-i-say-it-s-bad-it-s-bad">Sad Sunday (If I say it&#39;s bad, it&#39;s bad)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9785170814572" href="/book/show/18463675">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1638523813" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7003755012617253669">Despite my rating it's not a bad book. I didn't loose my head over it and it made me think quite a lot, but still, I expected something more. And I liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5558786.Metro_2033__METRO___1_' title='Metro 2033 (METRO, #1) by Dmitry Glukhovsky' rel='nofollow noopener'>Metro 2033</a> series way more. <br/><br/><b>Smells Like Orwell's Spirit (or Arm Pits)</b><br/><br/>For me, this book is very similar to G.Orwell's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5470.1984' title='1984 by George Orwell' rel='nofollow noopener'>1984</a>. It's sad, angry, melancholic. They both have this antagonist vs. protagonist (where the protagonist also IS the antagonist), man vs. the system topics, themes. In both books the government is the all-seeing and hearing Big </span>
  <span id="freeText7003755012617253669" style="display:none">Despite my rating it's not a bad book. I didn't loose my head over it and it made me think quite a lot, but still, I expected something more. And I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5558786.Metro_2033__METRO___1_" title="Metro 2033 (METRO, #1) by Dmitry Glukhovsky" rel="nofollow noopener">Metro 2033</a> series way more. <br><br><b>Smells Like Orwell's Spirit (or Arm Pits)</b><br><br>For me, this book is very similar to G.Orwell's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5470.1984" title="1984 by George Orwell" rel="nofollow noopener">1984</a>. It's sad, angry, melancholic. They both have this antagonist vs. protagonist (where the protagonist also IS the antagonist), man vs. the system topics, themes. In both books the government is the all-seeing and hearing Big Brother who wants to control everyone. If you are not with the System, you are out.<br><br>This book has a lot to offer. It also tackles family, damaged people, love, the dangers of living forever, struggles for power, rich/poor relationships. I also thing this book is also about impossible - in order to break everything, you have to sacrifice yourself. <br><br>I even expected the ending to be Orwellesque, but I was wrong. Even if, the ending was disappointing - it was too easy guessable if you read carefully and get all the hints. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444502108ra/16509832.gif" width="350" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Violence, violence everywhere</b><br><br>It's an angry, violent book. It made me feel uneasy, put some stones on my heart and mind. It's like a feverish dream - bright, burning, but also sad and deeply touching. I think some of the violence portrayed in the book was unnecessary - the main character sometimes just hits people who are a simple "background" without no particular reason from the author. Yeah, I get the fact that the main character is an uncaring asshole, but if he just punches everyone on the way home just out of the thin air it just looks and feels meh. <br><br>This book goes deep. To reader's mind, heart, muscles. Almost like it tries to overmaster you. It shows the picture of the world that is quite believable. It's "what if" book. Yet it made me wonder why most of the writers picture the future so dark. I am not an optimist, but I really hope the people of the future will manage. Somehow. Without pills, depression, monsters, alien attacks and etc. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464889472ra/19289302.gif" width="350" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Oh My Character</b><br><br>I don't know how I feel about main character. I don't hate him, but I dislike him. I know, that was authors intention, but with the all sad stories, backgrounds and unhappiness going on, I lost him. The theme of family is quite important in this book - at least fatherhood. The fact that only a child made him change (yeah, kids are the reason of life, yadadadada...) was a little... Fake? Seen before? Expected? Some of the drama was easily guessable. Some of the characters seemed based on stereotypes (Indians - happy and friendly, Pakistani - angry, Europeans - wealthy and etc.) Also, some of the other character's actions seemed weird and cray-cray. I was unable to connect actions with the reasons. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7003755012617253669" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1483225349" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1483225349" />
    <a title="Lorean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29980767-lorean"><img alt="Lorean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550611920p2/29980767.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1483225349?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lorean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lorean" href="/user/show/29980767-lorean">Lorean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9788024249179" href="/book/show/25925484-budoucnost">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29980767-lorean?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29980767-lorean?shelf=free-time-reading">free-time-reading</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1483225349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1276204637318428282">I haven’t read "Metro" yet so I can’t compare these books. But from my point of view, "Future" is an outstanding book in some way.<br/>Of course, it was pretty difficult to read - with all its brutality, violence and the whole idea of immortal overpopulated Europe. Also there‘re some social questions in the story which relate to current problems of our society. These things together make the book even more terrifying and I have to agree with people who compare this story to Orwell‘s "1984". <br/>What I re</span>
  <span id="freeText1276204637318428282" style="display:none">I haven’t read "Metro" yet so I can’t compare these books. But from my point of view, "Future" is an outstanding book in some way.<br />Of course, it was pretty difficult to read - with all its brutality, violence and the whole idea of immortal overpopulated Europe. Also there‘re some social questions in the story which relate to current problems of our society. These things together make the book even more terrifying and I have to agree with people who compare this story to Orwell‘s "1984". <br />What I really like about this book is the fact that there is no evil character. Of course, there’re good ones and bad ones but the evillest thing of the story is the Immortality itself. The Immortality which means you’ll stay young forever but sooner or later it will take your soul and you'll stop being human. The idea is awesome – mankind will live and have fun forever. But without our family, without children, without death – what are we going to live for?<br />The only thing I couldn’t stand was the rapid change of opinions of the main character. Actually, I like Jan Nachtigall as a "bad guy", a member of state police who destroys other people’s lives to protect Europe from absolute collapse. But when a particular woman character appears, all of the sudden he becomes naive and vulnerable, even after all those terrible things he had already gone through.. This is the reason why I didn’t like the main love story at first. But finally, I absolutely loved the ending. It maybe isn’t so epic as you expect. But Jan’s thoughts which are mentioned at the end of the story have so much power that you won’t be able to get them out of your head at least for a couple of days.<br />"Future" is a great dystopia. You’ll be super-depressed after reading the whole thing. But it’s definitely worth reading. Because the story has something that can destroy a part of you. And this destroyed part will give you another reason to live.<br /><br />EDIT 2017:<br />One year passed. I've just read Metro 2033 and I have to say - Future really is an extraordinary book. I'm not saying Metro is worse (not at all!). I found out that Future is simply &gt;different&lt; in some way. I loved this book and hated it at the same time. Honestly, reading it was one big struggle for me. However, after some time, I realized that there are still some questions to think about, if it comes to Future. Thus, I change my opinion. Not "a couple of days", you won't be able to get this book out of your head for YEARS. It was soo difficult for me to get along with this story. However, it was DAMN worth it.<br />I'm adding the fifth star. Awesome book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1276204637318428282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I wasn't expecting anything like it, so well done Mr. Gluhkovsky, well done indeed.</span>

<div id="review_1974182136" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1974182136" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1974182136?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angelika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angelika" href="/user/show/65840151-angelika">Angelika</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65840151-angelika?shelf=expectations-not-met">expectations-not-met</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65840151-angelika?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65840151-angelika?shelf=dystopian-utopian">dystopian-utopian</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65840151-angelika?shelf=terrible-mc">terrible-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65840151-angelika?shelf=adult-lit">adult-lit</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1974182136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11702548086693506982"><b>DNFed at page 160 of 630 (25%).</b><br/>1.5 star <br/><br/>Earlier this year I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17274667.Metro_2033__Metro___1_' title='Metro 2033 (Metro, #1) by Dmitry Glukhovsky' rel='nofollow noopener'>Metro 2033</a> and I fell in love. I adored everything about this book. The plot, the world building, the characters, the writing style... So as soon as I saw that there's another book by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3159299.Dmitry_Glukhovsky' title='Dmitry Glukhovsky' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dmitry Glukhovsky</a>, I ran to the library, positively shiting myself with glee. Good that I did, because I almost bought it. <br/><br/>I don't DNF books often, usually only if I can't bring myself to read another word, even if someone paid me. It's not that with </span>
  <span id="freeText11702548086693506982" style="display:none"><b>DNFed at page 160 of 630 (25%).</b><br />1.5 star <br /><br />Earlier this year I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17274667.Metro_2033__Metro___1_" title="Metro 2033 (Metro, #1) by Dmitry Glukhovsky" rel="nofollow noopener">Metro 2033</a> and I fell in love. I adored everything about this book. The plot, the world building, the characters, the writing style... So as soon as I saw that there's another book by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3159299.Dmitry_Glukhovsky" title="Dmitry Glukhovsky" rel="nofollow noopener">Dmitry Glukhovsky</a>, I ran to the library, positively shiting myself with glee. Good that I did, because I almost bought it. <br /><br />I don't DNF books often, usually only if I can't bring myself to read another word, even if someone paid me. It's not that with this one, I think I COULD continue, it's just that reading this book feels more like a torture with no end in sight. If someone told me its get's a milion times better, maybe i'd pick it up again someday. But as of now, I'm not going to waste my time on something this infuriating.<br /><br />On the back of the book it's written that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17274667.Metro_2033__Metro___1_" title="Metro 2033 (Metro, #1) by Dmitry Glukhovsky" rel="nofollow noopener">Metro 2033</a> was written by a boy, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27300577.FUTU_RE" title="FUTU.RE by Dmitry Glukhovsky" rel="nofollow noopener">FUTU.RE</a> was written by a man. If being a man means inserting rape, sex scenes, sexism and homophobia every five pages, then I think I'll pass. I mostly skimmed through the most graphic scenes, but they kept and kept reapearing. The main character kept objectifying every woman he met. He kept calling them sluts and whores. He kept being shitty towards gay men he met (even though it was said homosexuality was pretty normalised by then). I skimmed through the rest of the book, hoping he'd redeem himself at some point. I understand he had a reason to feel homophobic, I really do. But I thought he'd become an overal better person by the end of the book. And what do I find? By the page 500 something he still calls women sluts and still assumes every gay man is a prostitute! I know the author is russian, but come on. And he had guts to talk about Oscar Wilde at the beginning. He even had guts to call one of the characters after a character from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5297.The_Picture_of_Dorian_Gray" title="The Picture of Dorian Gray by Oscar Wilde" rel="nofollow noopener">The Picture of Dorian Gray</a>. But still, I tried to continue. But then I saw the metaphore he used, comparing chapels on hills to pierced nipples on a woman's breast. And I threw this garbage across the room. I'm sorry, but I'm furious. This is one of the most offensive pieces of writing I've ever seen.<br /><br />I liked the first chapter, the premise was amazing, but then it all went to shit. I'm giving this back to the library as soon as I can, because I don't want to look at it. Half a star because of really good world building.</span>

<div id="review_1292303749" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="László Takács" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4860318-l-szl-tak-cs"><img alt="László Takács" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452634165p2/4860318.jpg" /></a>

        <a title="László Takács" class="user" itemprop="url" name="László Takács" href="/user/show/4860318-l-szl-tak-cs">László Takács</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9785170814572" href="/book/show/18463675">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1292303749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4322830691826128898">A unique and disturbing dystopia.<br/>The book tries to answer the following question:<br/>What happens if immortality is reachable for everyone?<br/>Glukhovsky gives us a very sad answer.<br/><br/>So what you get if you read this book:<br/>- cruelty and violence<br/>- a scumbag main character<br/>- an 'okay' story and writing style<br/>- pure realism<br/>- some philosophy about the odds and ends of immortality and mortality<br/> <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[What is the meaning of life, if you are immortal? <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/>Personally, I don't really like this nove</span>
  <span id="freeText4322830691826128898" style="display:none">A unique and disturbing dystopia.<br />The book tries to answer the following question:<br />What happens if immortality is reachable for everyone?<br />Glukhovsky gives us a very sad answer.<br /><br />So what you get if you read this book:<br />- cruelty and violence<br />- a scumbag main character<br />- an 'okay' story and writing style<br />- pure realism<br />- some philosophy about the odds and ends of immortality and mortality<br /> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What is the meaning of life, if you are immortal? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Personally, I don't really like this novel. After you read this, you'll definitaly hate life. Too much terror in it and I don't like the characters.<br />I think Dmitry Glukhovsky has many good novels with mystical elements, irony and realism, but not this one.</span>

<div id="review_1851660612" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1851660612" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12353805-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518454186p2/12353805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1851660612?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/12353805-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12353805-carol?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12353805-carol?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1851660612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9956520108199961266">There's a lot of good things about this book, and others that aren't quite so. It's a harsh book, with lots of violence that makes the reading uncomfortable at times, but considering the kind of dystopian society I'm presented with, I wasn't expecting a cozy read either. I would've liked it to be shorter though, 626 pages to talk about this seemed a little excessive, because this is not the first book I read which talks about an 'immortal society' and how we've conquered death. It's not a new to</span>
  <span id="freeText9956520108199961266" style="display:none">There's a lot of good things about this book, and others that aren't quite so. It's a harsh book, with lots of violence that makes the reading uncomfortable at times, but considering the kind of dystopian society I'm presented with, I wasn't expecting a cozy read either. I would've liked it to be shorter though, 626 pages to talk about this seemed a little excessive, because this is not the first book I read which talks about an 'immortal society' and how we've conquered death. It's not a new topic, and I've seen it done in as little as 100 pages.<br /><br />***POSSIBLE SPOILERS AHEAD, READ WITH CAUTION***<br /><br />The story is about a society where people no longer die, so it is sold to you as a Utopia, where everyone is to remain young forever. But, this comes at a price, it is evident that no country will be able to hold an ever growing society, specially if peope don't die anymore, so what Europe has come up with as a solution is to allow every citizen the right to immortality, because it's a human right, however, should you bear children, you only have two options, either abort and keep your immortality, or have the kid at the cost of one parent giving up immortality. The legal way to do this is by registering a pregnancy and deciding which parent will receive an injection that will age them in a lapse of no more than 10 years, while the other parent is allowed to keep immortality and remain with the child. The idea is that, you pay a life with another life, because overpopulation is not an option and thre is no more space to live. <br /><br />The problem that was tackled in the book however is the illegal pregancies of course. This happens to be a huge problem in this society, because women get pregnant and they can't will themselves to register it because they don't want to die, and they don't want to lose their husbands either. So our main character, Jan, he is part of a special force called the Immortals, whose only task is to catch those illegal pregancies, inject one of the parents with the aging virus and then, since this was illegal, they take away the children to orphanages, where they will be trained to become the future Immortals. <br /><br />Jan actually comes from an orphanage, because his mother didn't register the pregnancy, and due to the horrible treatment he had there, he hates her, and he also hates all women. To him they are nothing but selfish whores, and he reminds you constantly of this. He is a horrible person and as a character you do get to hate him a lot, to me it was terribly uncomfortable to read his thoughts all the time, but when you start getting flashbacks of his life in the orphanage, you kinda understand why he is so horrible. He's had a terrible life that could've been avoided, but he doesn't understand why his mother never registered the pregnancy. He just doesn't understand what it is to have a kid, and what it means to have to give him up, because in the society he lives in both kids and old people are an abomination and the direct result of a crime.<br /><br />Throughout the book he will eventually change and grow as a character, he is told to kill the leader of the Party of Life, who keeps fighting for the right to reproduce, and to kill his girlfriend too, something he finds himself unable to do. And we will see him fall in love and eventually start changing his attitudes towards reproduction. It's a very slow change, and his mind goes crazy half the time because he can't deal with all the change that is happening in his life. There are many amazing plot twists, specially towards the end of the book, but there is also a lot of violence too, specially towards women (so do take it into account if you plan on reading this). <br /><br />It is still an interesting read because you get to see how selfish people become once they get immortality, and you also get to see the problems that you start having from a stagnant society. It was good, yes, very good. But it was also terribly long. I felt many of the discussions Jan had with himself in his head could have been avoided or even shorter. There are many chapters where nothing happens and too many descriptions. This would've been great with a good 200 pages less.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9956520108199961266" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10169331322326060562">Hands down the best book I've read this year. Mind is officially blown!! I don't know how I'm supposed to move on from this. Highly, highly recommend to everyone!!!!</span>

<div id="review_1664414580" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1664414580" />
    <a title="cloudsniffer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5478524-cloudsniffer"><img alt="cloudsniffer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452447872p2/5478524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1664414580?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="cloudsniffer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="cloudsniffer" href="/user/show/5478524-cloudsniffer">cloudsniffer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788363944483" href="/book/show/24842649-futu-re">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478524-cloudsniffer?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1664414580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17784410949971930213">Do you know why I hate horrors?<br/><br/>I can never get scared by the ghosts, or vampires, or zombies, or insert-any-existing-supernatural-entity.<br/>When I walk the dark alley alone I am not scared by ghost grabbing my ankle. <br/>But I am often terrified by humans. A drunk girl looking at me sideways as if she wanted to mangle and rob me. A shady guy sending me long glances <br/>No, I am never scared by the supernatural. It is human nature (or rather dark aspects of it) which makes me frightened.<br/><br/>That’s why I prefer </span>
  <span id="freeText17784410949971930213" style="display:none">Do you know why I hate horrors?<br /><br />I can never get scared by the ghosts, or vampires, or zombies, or insert-any-existing-supernatural-entity.<br />When I walk the dark alley alone I am not scared by ghost grabbing my ankle. <br />But I am often terrified by humans. A drunk girl looking at me sideways as if she wanted to mangle and rob me. A shady guy sending me long glances <br />No, I am never scared by the supernatural. It is human nature (or rather dark aspects of it) which makes me frightened.<br /><br />That’s why I prefer dystopias to horrors. You may claim that they are not scary, but I always feel cold, deep rooted dread when reading the books akin to Brave New World, 1984 or Lord of the Flies. It’s what-ifs that scare me, the possibility that we may give-in to the darkness which lays at the foundation of our nature and the society.<br /><br />I was delighted, when I found out that author of my beloved Metro 2033 has written serious dystopian novel. I loved both characters and worldbuilding in his postapocalyptic series and was looking forward how it will translate into more demanding enviroment<br /><br />How did it turn out?<br /><br />I saw people calling it Gluhovsky’s opus magnum. Truthfully, it does feel like he tried to create something bigger and more ambitious with this book. It is well thought, consistent and has a clear message. Yet there is one big issue which undermines some of it. <br /><br />It may not be book’s fault but mine. I tend to expect from novels set in dystopian one of the two things - either fast paced action in the interesting background or extensive study of human morality and nature. I don’t mind mixing these elements but it has to be done skillfully so that neither would be dilluted by the other one. Here, unfortunately it did not work as good. While FUTU.RE contains both of these, it seems like it can’t decide at times which of them it would like to show off to the reader. Psychological, social and moral elements are presented in a rather naive way. Gluhovsky spends too much time on the issue of reproducion, ignoring all other aspects. Socioeconomic stagnation? Lack of innovations due to the more or less static population? Or perhaps the fact that the human brain is not designed to live forever and can hold only limited amount of information? I can write the whole list and it still would be just scrathching the surface. I mean, I get it, the book wanted to fit a problem into certain narration. But the problem of possible immortality is much more complex than simple biological need for reproduction and ignoring other possible problems is just too much of a simplification. <br /><br />Outside of the main character - Jan, the cast is pretty bland and one dimensional but they serve their purpose. Unfortunately the main big bad guy is pretty obvious from the beginning (and the intrigue not so . The childhood enemy has no other history beside the one connected with the main character. Annelie was pretty illogical character as she dealt with what happened to her way too quickly. The only one character which I truly came to care about was Helen who seemed to be the most courageous and strong despite her situation.<br />As for Jan, I hated him as a person, yet I liked him as a character from whose perspective we got to know the world in FUTU.RE. At first he was very set on the principles of the european order then as his character developed, so did the narration<br /><br />Still, I found the ending quite disappointing.Honestly with the way the final part was heading, I expected ending to be similar to the 1984. It wasn’t. It was anticlimatic. And, oh, so badly thought in comparison with the rest of the novel. I mean I may not be a fan of the happy endings in this genre, but I could swallow it here. I could if it was not for a little single fact. Jan had no proof that the vial contained that he thought it did. Not. A. Single. Proof. I know, that the scene when he obtained it was set so that we would assume that he was not lied to. But still, it bugs me and makes me want to scream, that this would make a perfect plot twist. The one which would be so much more fitting.<br /><br />Nevertheless this is a solid book. It has a great world building and characters, despite being often one dimensional, are still believable and easy to like (or hate). It’s even better if you are starting with the ‘serious’ dystopian literature - as its watered down moral dilemma and not-so grim dark ending may be easier to swallow than in some. <br />Definitely recommended if you are dystopia or Gluhovsky’s fan<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17784410949971930213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1697233414" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1697233414" />
    <a title="Plamen Nenchev" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39368861-plamen-nenchev"><img alt="Plamen Nenchev" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599945372p2/39368861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1697233414?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Plamen Nenchev" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Plamen Nenchev" href="/user/show/39368861-plamen-nenchev">Plamen Nenchev</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9788445002056" href="/book/show/22032765-futu-re">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39368861-plamen-nenchev?shelf=pathetic">pathetic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1697233414" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11234088188177077025">Ever since the immensely entertaining Metro 2033, I have followed Glukhovsky's attempts at new books, however ill-fated they have been. Until this book, which is not just bad, but plainly offensive.<br/><br/>Futu.re takes place in Europe in the 25th century which is a "paradise come true", but – and we learn this in the very first pages – there is something really, really rotten about it. The good protagonist is absolutely sure about it. And Europe is not only rotten, but also very much Gayrope. Gays are </span>
  <span id="freeText11234088188177077025" style="display:none">Ever since the immensely entertaining Metro 2033, I have followed Glukhovsky's attempts at new books, however ill-fated they have been. Until this book, which is not just bad, but plainly offensive.<br /><br />Futu.re takes place in Europe in the 25th century which is a "paradise come true", but – and we learn this in the very first pages – there is something really, really rotten about it. The good protagonist is absolutely sure about it. And Europe is not only rotten, but also very much Gayrope. Gays are running wild in the streets, they rape the protagonist when he is a kid, grope him on the train, ogle him in the street – like rabid dogs they are. Gayrope is not only full of gays but also generally degenerated, immoral and wanton. The protagonist naturally is above these things, he is deeply disgusted by them and takes every chance he gets to kick and beat up these degenerates, whether they are men, women, gays, children, whatever!<br /><br />For such a "Gayropean" setting, the protagonist, his actions and everyone around him look rather Russian. I have read enough Russian books to know what I am talking about. If this had been a good novel, I could have compared him to some of Dostoyevsky's quirkiest (alcoholic) characters, but such distinction is out of the question here. The protagonist is mad at everything and everyone, wants to kick everything and everyone and continuously has episodes that can only be described in medical terms. But the author keeps insisting he is a good guy. Yeah, right.<br /><br />So – to make long things short – Europe is Gayrope, disgusting, immoral and rotten, and the main protagonist – who is not Russian but awfully looks like one – will fight to the end to "make things right". What does this look to you? To me it looks like Russian government propaganda.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11234088188177077025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText270622646461615312" style="display:none">A VERRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRRY long book, that is quite intriguing and has a lot of memorable moments, but as you can tell by my initial reaction I think it could have been about three times shorter.               >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer440728046673119483">In the future death has been defeated and everyone became immortal. This lead to the demographic catastrophe and soon having kids became illegal. <br/>The premise left me feeling that I’ve already seen this somewhere. A person who is a part of the system starts seeing how it became corrupt and turned against it. <br/>The plot left me wondering why was there no space colonization?   <span id="freeText440728046673119483" style="display:none">In the future death has been defeated and everyone became immortal. This lead to the demographic catastrophe and soon having kids became illegal. <br />The premise left me feeling that I’ve already seen this somewhere. A person who is a part of the system starts seeing how it became corrupt and turned against it. <br />The plot left me wondering why was there no space colonization? Why was there a severe punishment for having kids but no sterilization took place? I guess all of this did not serve the plot well. <br />This book takes a look into the uncontrolled immigration, demographic issues, political corruption, idealism and love. I think it was too expanded and the premise left me wondering about some missing logical points. </span>
  <a data-text-id="440728046673119483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2741065699" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2741065699" />
    <a title="Deni Jane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44616913-deni-jane"><img alt="Deni Jane" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2741065699?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deni Jane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deni Jane" href="/user/show/44616913-deni-jane">Deni Jane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2741065699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12359082566738541609">"Future" is my first book by Glukhovsky and it was a long awaited treat, ever since I read the synopsis of the book and put it on my "must-read" list. So when I finally found the time to read it, I had really high expectations. <br/>Well, the book didn't disappoint me. Although I'm not a fan of writers who rely too much on sexual violence and gore to impress the reader, the world building won me. The book is incredibly well thought of. Excluding the little "I hate Russia" part, which felt a bit too p</span>
  <span id="freeText12359082566738541609" style="display:none">"Future" is my first book by Glukhovsky and it was a long awaited treat, ever since I read the synopsis of the book and put it on my "must-read" list. So when I finally found the time to read it, I had really high expectations. <br />Well, the book didn't disappoint me. Although I'm not a fan of writers who rely too much on sexual violence and gore to impress the reader, the world building won me. The book is incredibly well thought of. Excluding the little "I hate Russia" part, which felt a bit too personal and not so logical, everything else is spot on. The world is both futuristic and very easy to imagine. Because all the vices of the modern world are extrapolated to a future without death. From the American market-above-all, to the European fake rights-for-everyone, to the eternal conflict between India and Pakistan, to the Chinese workforce, it all sounds so credible. It's so easy to imagine this world and so hard to accept the dark distopia as a possible future. And it certainly is a possible one. Among others, softer or nicer ones. <br />I don't accept the authors claim that we're not worthy of immortality. But I totally agree that death is the driving force in our civilization and without it, we'll need to reinvent our souls and our society. I find the focus on children to be a good symbol, but otherwise, oversimplification. The civilization doesn't move forward while you nurse a baby. But the civilization survives thanks to those babies. Children are the new hope, our final attempt to do something good with our lives, even if everything else has failed. They are the fresh copy of our hardware and software, that has the chance to do better than us. Our final message to the future. But if we are immortal, we don't need to leave a message, we can just wait for the future to come. <br />It's a really good book. Really dark, really disturbing, but a good study of that particular possible future. And it's very well written, very hard to put the book down, because the story is so enchanting and the characters are so interesting - both weird and so normal. I really wish there was a bit less sexual violence, though. Particularly considering that technology and the good life tends to make people less sexual, not more. For teenagers - ok, but for 50-100 years old, I don't think that would be such a driving force. But then who knows, people are strange creatures - the better the life, the crazier they tend to get. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12359082566738541609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It's our world hundreads of years into the future but it is the same hate, political games, and paid of media that exists on different levels today. <br /><br />Medical sciense is basiclly tossed out the window in this book because genetic modification has defeted death, basiclly no one dies, there is no diseasses, everyone is young and perfect forever. Your kids will be sent of to institues where they are controlled and trained into basiclly being assassins for the government. <br /><br />Overpopulation is the biggest threat of them all. If a person is born, one needs to die in order to make room for it. The economi, the housing, the system of which people live by would all fall apart if it were to change. But maybe that is what needs to happen. Maybe a revolution is needed. And sometimes the ones who brings the revolution is the most unlikely of them all? </span>

  <span id="freeText3564122544676319359" style="display:none">I read the previuos Metro books from the author so when i saw this at a bookstore i expected a well written work. The story looked interesting and the authors previuos works was great so i picked it up.<br /><br />I shouldnt have though. The book starts up strong with good character development and keeping the pace enough to keep the reader interested while still finding time to put philosophy in. The plotline can be somewhat predictable, but i was not expecting some mindbender from this. However after <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ when Jan leaves Barselona  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> the book takes a turn for the worse.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('44L4tQRrgNONMq+8wZju4e9+pBQ1CRy/VHhpvkMHiDOhlP4DFFLP3bksB1uVnU+iZySMVtip2BueLJt23JKkhA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7465903561479777620">Dmitry Glukhovsky (Russian: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6434478._' rel='nofollow noopener'>Дмитрий Глуховский</a>) is a professional Russian author and journalist. Glukhovsky started in 2002 by publishing his first novel, Metro 2033, on his own website to be viewed for free. The novel has later become an interactive experiment, drawing in many readers, and has since been made into a video game for the Xbox 360 console and PC. Glukhovsky is known in Russia for his</span>
  <span id="freeText7465903561479777620" style="display:none">Dmitry Glukhovsky (Russian: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6434478._" rel="nofollow noopener">Дмитрий Глуховский</a>) is a professional Russian author and journalist. Glukhovsky started in 2002 by publishing his first novel, Metro 2033, on his own website to be viewed for free. The novel has later become an interactive experiment, drawing in many readers, and has since been made into a video game for the Xbox 360 console and PC. Glukhovsky is known in Russia for his novels Metro 2033 and "It's Getting Darker". He is also an author of a series of satirical "Stories of Motherland" criticizing today's Russia.<br />As a journalist, Dmitry Glukhovsky has worked for EuroNews TV in France, Deutsche Welle, and RT. In 2008-2009 he worked as a radio host of a Mayak Radio Station. He writes columns for Harper’s Bazaar, l’Officiel and Playboy.<br />He has lived in Israel, Germany and France and speaks English, French, German, Hebrew and Spanish as well as his native Russian.</span>
